      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18385207906401775406">Georgette Heyer, the grande dame of Regencies, is considered the creator of the modern Regency genre. From her first book in 1935, she established herself as the expert in the field. Her books are hot commodities, especially since many of them have been out of print for some time.In July, Harlequin is pleased to present "The Corinthian", the sixth and final Georgette Heyer</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18385207906401775406">Georgette Heyer, the grande dame of Regencies, is considered the creator of the modern Regency genre. From her first book in 1935, she established herself as the expert in the field. Her books are hot commodities, especially since many of them have been out of print for some time.In July, Harlequin is pleased to present "The Corinthian", the sixth and final Georgette Heyer title that we will be publishing in 2000.<br /><br />The only question perplexing Sir Richard Wyndham is one of marriage. When he chances on a beautiful young fugitive climbing out of a window by means of knotted sheets, he realizes life is about to get very interesting!<br /><br />With a foreword by Kasey Michaels, a New York Times bestselling author of more than fifty books and recipient of the Romantic Times Magazine Career Achievement Award for Regency Historical novels.<br /><br />Watch your profits soar as readers look to complete their collection with this final title.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1267323823">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267323823" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="left imgcol" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1383845644p2/8734459.jpg" alt="Tadiana ? Night Owl?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1267323823?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="user" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?">Tadiana ? Night Owl?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6271224-the-corinthian" title="Paperback 9781402217692" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=squeaky-clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">squeaky-clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=whatever" class="actionLinkLite">whatever</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1267323823">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7549108777469821086">Sigh. I've done it again.<br /><br />I've overdosed on Georgette Heyer Regencies, and now I can't tell if I'm bored because this is mediocre Heyer or because I've reached saturation point on her books. The banter is witty, the hero capable and charming, the heroine brave and feisty, and I was pretty much unmoved by it all.<br /><br />It's a cute and humorous plot: Sir Richard Wyndham is just about to enter into an engagement with the cold woman everyone expects him to marry, and has gotten very drunk to drown his unhap</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7549108777469821086">Sigh. I've done it again.<br /><br />I've overdosed on Georgette Heyer Regencies, and now I can't tell if I'm bored because this is mediocre Heyer or because I've reached saturation point on her books. The banter is witty, the hero capable and charming, the heroine brave and feisty, and I was pretty much unmoved by it all.<br /><br />It's a cute and humorous plot: Sir Richard Wyndham is just about to enter into an engagement with the cold woman everyone expects him to marry, and has gotten very drunk to drown his unhappiness. He is making his boozy way home when he sees someone climbing out of a 2nd story window. Intrigued, he stops to catch this young person (since the knotted sheets they're climbing down stop several feet short of the ground). It turns out that this young person is 17 year old Penelope Cress, a wealthy orphan who is running away to avoid being pressured into marrying her cousin. The soused Sir Richard decides that running away sounds like a very good idea indeed, and, besides, Pen obviously needs someone older and capable to watch out for her.<br /><br />So off they go, Pen with short hair and dressed in boy's clothing. Various shenanigans ensue. Also hijinks. And love blossoms in places unexpected to the hero and heroine but certainly not to the reader. Pen thinks she's going to go formalize her 5 year old unofficial engagement to Piers Luttrell, an old buddy of hers (so she was 12 when she was hanging out and making a youthful marriage pact with this 16 year old boy? Okaaay, I'm not going to think about that too hard). Some of the funniest parts are what happens when they finally meet up with Piers and the silly, weepy girl he's currently involved with. There's also a stolen diamond necklace subplot to add to the craziness.<br /><br />Part of my problem is the age difference between Pen and Richard: 17 and 29. I'm past the point in my life where that's romantic to me, although I can handwave that if the rest of the story really grabs me. The romance is kind of given short shrift here, but that often happens with Heyer. Maybe I just wasn't in the mood for comedic escapades.<br /><br />3 so-so stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7549108777469821086">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1053694349">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053694349" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner" class="left imgcol" title="Ruth Turner"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435387851p2/17861817.jpg" alt="Ruth Turner" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1053694349?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner" class="user" title="Ruth Turner">Ruth Turner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17861817-ruth-turner?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1053694349">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18104603747316581622"><br />Georgette Heyer is my go-to author when I want something well written, light hearted and witty to read. She never disappoints.<br /><br />The Corinthian is one of my favourites. I liked Sir Richard immensely, and Pen was funny and charming and had me laughing out loud at times.<br /><br />There were many interesting secondary characters that appealed to me as well. I didn't find the "thieves cant" a problem as some other readers did. I think the story was better for including it.<br /><br />A quick and enjoyable read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_648998554">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648998554" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21428432-tweety" class="left imgcol" title="Tweety"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1415237964p2/21428432.jpg" alt="Tweety" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/648998554?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21428432-tweety" class="user" title="Tweety">Tweety</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6271224-the-corinthian" title="Paperback 9781402217692" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Heyer fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tweety by: </span>
      Several of my GR friends 
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=sweet-and-clean-g-to-pg" class="actionLinkLite">sweet-and-clean-g-to-pg</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=ebay-amazon" class="actionLinkLite">ebay-amazon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer648998554">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3746516242570129419"><strong>3 1/2</strong> <br /><br />I don't know what to think. The characters are top notch as usual with Heyer and the humor is as amusing as ever. But the plot! I don't know which part was more unbelievable. Penelope running away in men's clothing, the adventures by stagecoach or the elopement of one very silly secondary couple. <br /><br />I cringe to say this about my beloved Heyer. But I've got to say it. Of all her books that I have read, however far fetched they maybe, she makes it work. But this one takes the cake. And I don't</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3746516242570129419"><strong>3 1/2</strong> <br /><br />I don't know what to think. The characters are top notch as usual with Heyer and the humor is as amusing as ever. But the plot! I don't know which part was more unbelievable. Penelope running away in men's clothing, the adventures by stagecoach or the elopement of one very silly secondary couple. <br /><br />I cringe to say this about my beloved Heyer. But I've got to say it. Of all her books that I have read, however far fetched they maybe, she makes it work. But this one takes the cake. And I don't think it worked for me. I enjoyed it, don't get me wrong, but I couldn't believe it. Her other books felt more likely, even when they were unusual situations, this one just didn't do that for me. If I could have gotten past my disbelief it would have been fine. I just kept seeing this as if it was really happening and saying "No, No, No! Not in a million years!" However, truth is stranger than fiction so no doubt in a different mood I could read this without any qualms. I really think the bizarre case with the Bow Street Runner was really too much. <br /><br />The Good, <br />My favorite character was a scamp. Cedric, the drunkard, the sponge and completely humorous pest. He was quite honest about his faults, on one occasion he told the Richard not to marry his sister and that if he did marry his sister he, Cedric would sponge off him for the rest of his days and that if Richard married her despite his warning he would be a greater fool than he'd thought. <br /><br />Richard was definitely a Corinthian. In fact I didn't like him much to start since he was so into his dratted cloths. By the end I did, but just not enough to raise my rating. I found him easily amused which I liked, since it unbuttoned him a bit. Overall thought, not a fav. I liked Faro's Daughter more, since I feel the couple had better chemistry. Speaking of which, this book only covers about a weeks worth of time. <br /><br />Pen, she was adorable, if reckless and terribly innocent. Also, she is wonderfully sure of herself, she has a magnificent imagination. The stories she comes up with! So mind blowing and nearly always funny. She and Cedric are the life of the book and I just wish the plot had been a a bit different so I could enjoy it more. <br /><br />Anyway, go into this book expecting bizarre, ridiculous and unrealistic but humorous adventures with a wild young chap called "Pen" <br /><br /><br /><strong>PG</strong> nearly no violence,few swears and the only thing bumping this up to a PG is that some people may not like that at the end the hero kisses Penelope who is still in boys cloths in front of a stagecoach full of people. I admit that felt kinda silly to me. Just unrealistic I guess. But, it fiction so enjoy the ride!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3746516242570129419">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067926528" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4368838-caz" class="left imgcol" title="Caz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332962126p2/4368838.jpg" alt="Caz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1067926528?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 19, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4368838-caz" class="user" title="Caz">Caz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/23001961-the-corinthian" title="Audible Audio " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-regency" class="actionLinkLite">romance-regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=4-5-stars" class="actionLinkLite">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=oldies-but-goodies" class="actionLinkLite">oldies-but-goodies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=aar" class="actionLinkLite">aar</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-1800-1850" class="actionLinkLite">romance-1800-1850</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1067926528">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13713573369896083435"><strong>I've given this an A+ for narration and B+ for content at AAR, so probably nearer 5 stars than 4.</strong><br /><br />One of the best things about listening to new audio versions of older books is becoming reacquainted with stories I read many more years ago than I care to count! Georgette Heyer’s <strong>The Corinthian</strong> is not a title I’ve re-read over the years, so coming back to it in audio was almost like experiencing a new book. And a terrific experience it was!<br /><br />The story is one with which any regular Regency reader is p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13713573369896083435"><strong>I've given this an A+ for narration and B+ for content at AAR, so probably nearer 5 stars than 4.</strong><br /><br />One of the best things about listening to new audio versions of older books is becoming reacquainted with stories I read many more years ago than I care to count! Georgette Heyer’s <strong>The Corinthian</strong> is not a title I’ve re-read over the years, so coming back to it in audio was almost like experiencing a new book. And a terrific experience it was!<br /><br />The story is one with which any regular Regency reader is probably very familiar: an older, sophisticated and somewhat ennui-laden man-about-town becomes accidentally embroiled in a hare-brained scheme perpetrated by a younger female. One thing leads to another, in the way of a cartoon snowball rolling down a mountainside, and the couple ends up in the middle of all sorts of madness and mayhem while falling in love.<br /><br />That’s pretty much the plot of The Corinthian - with more laughs, obviously. Handsome and extremely wealthy, twenty-nine year-old Sir Richard Wyndham is constantly pressured by his family to hasten his betrothal to the lovely, demure and very proper Honourable Melissa Brandon, who, they keep telling him, will make him the perfect wife. Unable to postpone the inevitable any longer and intending to propose the next day, Richard goes out and gets drunk and, on the way home, stops to assist a young lad climbing out of a window. The boy turns out (naturally) to be a very feminine armful, Miss Penelope Creed. Penelope - or Pen - is running away from her aunt and uncle to escape their plot to marry her to her fish-faced cousin to keep her large dowry in the family.<br /><br />Pen tells Richard she owns a house in Somerset and intends to make her way there to seek the help of a childhood friend. She is about to turn and leave, but Richard is not quite drunk enough for his common sense to have completely abandoned him. He insists that Pen can’t possibly wander the streets of London alone, late at night, dressed as a boy and tells her he will escort her to Somerset. On their journey, the pair cross paths with a jewel thief, a Bow Street Runner and even a dead body, and Richard finds himself having to constantly think on his feet to be able to keep up with Pen’s seemingly endless capacity for spinning yarns and finding trouble – and finds himself having the most fun he’s ever had in his life. <br /><br />You can read the rest of this review at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.likesbooks.com/cgi-bin/bookReview.pl?BookReviewId=10353">All About Romance</a><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_581432786">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581432786" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="left imgcol" title="Anne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437261844p2/18780551.jpg" alt="Anne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/581432786?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="user" title="Anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6271224-the-corinthian" title="Paperback 9781402217692" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=young-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">young-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=gentleman-like-heroes" class="actionLinkLite">gentleman-like-heroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer581432786">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6656554187457594462">Curiously, I did not enjoy this novel as much as I had expected to. I really really liked it, but I didn't get the same kind of satisfactory and awesome feeling I got after reading "The Black Moth" and "Powder and Patch" by the same author. The story, although good, seemed too unbelievable, which made the characters appear awkward as a whole, though I loved them individually. Sir Richard was a perfect, Heyer-typical hero and I thought the character of Penelope to be vastly entertaining. She was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6656554187457594462">Curiously, I did not enjoy this novel as much as I had expected to. I really really liked it, but I didn't get the same kind of satisfactory and awesome feeling I got after reading "The Black Moth" and "Powder and Patch" by the same author. The story, although good, seemed too unbelievable, which made the characters appear awkward as a whole, though I loved them individually. Sir Richard was a perfect, Heyer-typical hero and I thought the character of Penelope to be vastly entertaining. She was honest, sincere, naïve and innocent and offered a good contrast with Sir Richard. I loved the way she handled Lydia's affairs and the way she reacted to Lydia's general behaviour! Those parts were really funny.<br />I think what really threw me off was the ending... the romance, though predictable seem to come out of nowhere and it felt random and out of place. I liked the match, but I would have loved to have been given any ideas earlier that it was going to happen. But too much was focused on the mystery part of the novel, which didn't leave room for romantic interludes. Also, the ending did not feel conclusive at all, I felt like a whole chapter was missing!<br />Overall, I still strongly recommend it, but wouldn't recommend as a Heyer first read. It sill features amongst the best books I have ever read, but it's not Heyer's best.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/11488136-lynn-spencer" class="user" title="Lynn Spencer">Lynn Spencer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6271224-the-corinthian" title="Paperback 9781402217692" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11488136-lynn-spencer?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11488136-lynn-spencer?shelf=traditional-regency-romance" class="actionLinkLite">traditional-regency-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1454408910">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13799681884701610048"><strong>4.5 stars</strong> Oh, that was so much fun!<br /><br />I don't usually go for "chick in pants" romances, but this one was exceptionally well done. The fashionable Sir Richard Wyndham is desperately seeking a way out of offering marriage to the icy Melissa Brandon. Not only does she fail to appeal to him(his family has wanted the two to marry for <em>years</em>), but her feckless family seems to be tumbling into financial ruin.<br /><br />Penelope Creed is trying to escape as well. While Richard's family has been trying to browbeat him</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13799681884701610048"><strong>4.5 stars</strong> Oh, that was so much fun!<br /><br />I don't usually go for "chick in pants" romances, but this one was exceptionally well done. The fashionable Sir Richard Wyndham is desperately seeking a way out of offering marriage to the icy Melissa Brandon. Not only does she fail to appeal to him(his family has wanted the two to marry for <em>years</em>), but her feckless family seems to be tumbling into financial ruin.<br /><br />Penelope Creed is trying to escape as well. While Richard's family has been trying to browbeat him into marrying Melissa, her aunt has been trying to force heiress Penelope to marry her son.<br /><br />It all comes to a head when Penelope dresses as a boy and tries to climb out of her window. Richard, passing by, rescues her and very quickly sees through her disguise. He eventually helps her improve her disguise and the two go off together as uncle and nephew (or tutor and student, or any of several other ruses) on a journey to return Penelope to her home, where she thinks she will be welcomed with open arms.<br /><br />Along the way we encounter an odd variety of fellow travellers, jewel thieves and murder. There is also hilarious dialogue and a bit of romance. The story isn't even vaguely realistic, but it's great comedy. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/2411388-hannah" class="user" title="Hannah">Hannah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=regencys" class="actionLinkLite">regencys</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer61494961">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16649475193157075509">Second Heyer I read, and much better then Faro's Daughter IMO. Pen was a very delightful heroine, and I felt Heyer did a much better job developing the budding romance between Pen and Richard then she did with the main characters in Faro's Daughter.<br /><br />The plot was engaging and well maintained throughout the book, full of the types of adventures you'd expect to find in a regency (i.e. struggles against marriages of convenience, a bored yet lonely dandy, a girl disguised as a boy). I did have a bit o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16649475193157075509">Second Heyer I read, and much better then Faro's Daughter IMO. Pen was a very delightful heroine, and I felt Heyer did a much better job developing the budding romance between Pen and Richard then she did with the main characters in Faro's Daughter.<br /><br />The plot was engaging and well maintained throughout the book, full of the types of adventures you'd expect to find in a regency (i.e. struggles against marriages of convenience, a bored yet lonely dandy, a girl disguised as a boy). I did have a bit of a problem trying to understand some of the thief "cant" from the character of Jimmy Yarde, but kudos to Heyer for having it in there - it added to the period feel, although it was fairly incomprehensible to my 2009 American ears! Heyer even managed to flesh out some very minor characters introduced during a coach trip and make them funny and clearly drawn - it was probably my favorite part of the novel, although the last paragraph had me in stitches as well, I must say - read it and find out for yourself why!<br /><br />I will definitely read more Heyers, and hope I can find another with the brightness and engaging characters of The Corinthian.<br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="user" title="Olga Godim">Olga Godim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268155391">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13737887848616450819">This book is a treasure trove of laughter. It should be used in laugh therapy. <br />Sir Richard Wyndham is a twenty-nine-year-old Corinthian – wealthy, sophisticated, handsome, and supremely bored with his untroubled, aristocratic existence. He boxes like a champion, drives his horses like an Apollo, and dresses to the nines. <br />He has only one gripe: his mother and sister keep accosting him to get married. He doesn’t wish to, so he drowns his gloom in brandy. Later, after getting ultimately drunk, he w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13737887848616450819">This book is a treasure trove of laughter. It should be used in laugh therapy. <br />Sir Richard Wyndham is a twenty-nine-year-old Corinthian – wealthy, sophisticated, handsome, and supremely bored with his untroubled, aristocratic existence. He boxes like a champion, drives his horses like an Apollo, and dresses to the nines. <br />He has only one gripe: his mother and sister keep accosting him to get married. He doesn’t wish to, so he drowns his gloom in brandy. Later, after getting ultimately drunk, he wanders the streets of London and wallows in self-pity, until he catches a girl, seventeen-year-old Pen Creed, dangling out of a window of her aunt’s house on a too short a sheet. <br />Pen, disguised as a boy, is set on avoiding a distasteful marriage to her cousin, who “has a face like a fish.” She wants to have an adventure.<br />From the moment she falls into Richard’s arms, boredom becomes the least of his worries. Pen, an enterprising young woman, enmeshes them both in a series of crazy imbroglios. As soon as they escape a thief, they get saddled with a stolen diamond necklace. Then Pen’s aunt comes in pursuit, and Richard has no choice but to lie to the shrewish woman. Then an irate father of a neighborhood beauty accuses Pen, who is still dressed as a boy, of trifling with his innocent daughter. Then a Bow Street runner almost claps Pen in jail. You get the drift. <br />Richard has his hands full with his mischievous charge. With poise and patience, he extricates her from one scrape after another, but the more time he spends with Pen, the deeper he tumbles in love with her. She is friendly and compassionate, naïve and resourceful. Always full of hair-raising ideas, she lets her imagination fly unfettered and charms the socks out of the world-weary playboy Richard. Without meaning to, she teaches him to enjoy life again. <br />These two protagonists dance a merry gavotte around each other. She pretends he is her uncle/tutor/cousin/trustee and treats him with easy affection. She doesn’t even realize she is in love with him until the very end. He knows his mind earlier in the story but can’t declare his heart because he wouldn’t take advantage of an inexperienced girl. <br />To this charismatic duo, the author added a dozen eccentric secondary characters and a plot that wounds itself like a demented corkscrew, full of absurd allegation and mistaken identities. The dialog is fast and witty, and the food, as always in Heyer’s novels, is delicious. Together, they form the best recipe for a light and sparkly literary masterpiece.<br />Definitely one of the best Heyer’s novels. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13737887848616450819">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/897073-angela" class="user" title="Angela">Angela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer88042888">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12873329504770394009">Though I wasn't initially engaged with the rather drawn-out and verbose beginning, I quickly found myself hooked into one of Heyer's most madcap adventures of those I have read (on par, or even more outrageous than <a title="The Grand Sophy by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261689.The_Grand_Sophy">The Grand Sophy</a>). Despite the convoluted plot and rather tenuous role of chance threading its way through the novel, I enjoyed myself immensely.<br /><br />The two main characters are wonderfully written, with more believable motives and character arcs than the otherwise fantastic story would see</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12873329504770394009">Though I wasn't initially engaged with the rather drawn-out and verbose beginning, I quickly found myself hooked into one of Heyer's most madcap adventures of those I have read (on par, or even more outrageous than <a title="The Grand Sophy by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261689.The_Grand_Sophy">The Grand Sophy</a>). Despite the convoluted plot and rather tenuous role of chance threading its way through the novel, I enjoyed myself immensely.<br /><br />The two main characters are wonderfully written, with more believable motives and character arcs than the otherwise fantastic story would seem to support. I agree with other reviewers that, in our day, a romance with a 12-year age disparity feels rather awkward - even inappropriate - but I think Heyer pulled it off just fine. I would recommend this book to regency fans in general, and Heyer fans in particular.<br /><br />I should add that my favorable impression was increased by the fact that I listened to this book on CD; it was read by Eve Matthison, who gave a fantastic performance and added wonderful inflection, accents, and emotion to the story. I recommend this version even more than the hard copy.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/20698-larissa?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20698-larissa?shelf=humor-satire" class="actionLinkLite">humor-satire</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20698-larissa?shelf=english" class="actionLinkLite">english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1413958310">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer234450064102489924">Following a rather grueling month of translating projects at school and facing a very long journey from Iceland to Maine, I decided it was obviously time for a 'fun read' and was persuaded, by <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.tor.com/2013/01/15/creating-a-sub-genre-by-accident-georgette-heyers-the-corinthian/">this</a>very enjoyable and informative post about Georgette Heyer's inadvertent creation of the Regency Romance genre, to pick up <em>The Corinthian</em>. <br /><br />As with many of Heyer's books, this one presents a number of variations on themes and characters that she would pick up again and again throughout her career (althou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText234450064102489924">Following a rather grueling month of translating projects at school and facing a very long journey from Iceland to Maine, I decided it was obviously time for a 'fun read' and was persuaded, by <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.tor.com/2013/01/15/creating-a-sub-genre-by-accident-georgette-heyers-the-corinthian/">this</a>very enjoyable and informative post about Georgette Heyer's inadvertent creation of the Regency Romance genre, to pick up <em>The Corinthian</em>. <br /><br />As with many of Heyer's books, this one presents a number of variations on themes and characters that she would pick up again and again throughout her career (although it was, to be fair, the originator of many of these themes). Here, our May-December romance is comprised of a large, "sleepy" hero who favors dandy-ish fashion and yet is no one to be trifled with; Richard, we're told, is apparently a renowned "whip" (he's good with horses), a fearsome boxer, and is very handy with his pistols—although we never see the latter two talents in action. We also have his young(er), plucky heroine who has a knack for getting into trouble, who rallies the hero out of his boredom and staid habits, and who favors boys' clothing. There are also stolen jewels, murder, masked bandits, and Bow Street Runners in the mix. It's all a lot of fun, although not nearly as sharp with the dialog or as delightfully convoluted as <em>The Masqueraders</em>, for instance. But it was a great way to while away a long journey, and it's interesting, I think, to see how Heyer got started in a genre she'd go on to perfect. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="234450064102489924">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_423493591">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423493591" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11349024-becca" class="left imgcol" title="Becca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423870283p2/11349024.jpg" alt="Becca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/423493591?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11349024-becca" class="user" title="Becca">Becca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6271224-the-corinthian" title="Paperback 9781402217692" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11349024-becca?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer423493591">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11191340284616682588">I have previously heard Georgette Heyer described as the “Queen of Regency Romance”, and after having read <em>The Corinthian</em>, I am now fully convinced that this is indeed the case. This is the fourth novel of Georgette Heyer’s that I have encountered… and incidentally the first one I’ve encountered in paperback. Thus this particular novel proved that I do (as I had thought) greatly enjoy Ms Heyer’s delightful stories; and that it wasn’t only because Richard Armitage narrated the three other stories</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11191340284616682588">I have previously heard Georgette Heyer described as the “Queen of Regency Romance”, and after having read <em>The Corinthian</em>, I am now fully convinced that this is indeed the case. This is the fourth novel of Georgette Heyer’s that I have encountered… and incidentally the first one I’ve encountered in paperback. Thus this particular novel proved that I do (as I had thought) greatly enjoy Ms Heyer’s delightful stories; and that it wasn’t only because Richard Armitage narrated the three other stories that I enjoy her work excessively. I’m not saying that having Richard Armitage reading it wouldn’t have made <em>The Corinthian</em> more enjoyable, but hey, you can’t have everything. <br /><br />The book starts out following the movements of Sir Richard Wyndham, the Corinthian, who is being beleaguered by his relatives to offer for Melissa Brandon. I don’t blame him for not wanting to marry her; honestly, I was so disgusted by her character, the only difference between Melissa and a marble statue is that Melissa could breathe. Sir Richard’s character seemed to me to be vaguely reminiscent of the Earl of Rule from <em>The Convenient Marriage</em>, (incidentally one of my favourite Georgette Heyer novels), but upon further study it appeared it was only the presence of his odious sister that made him seem so. I believe one of the things I like most about Georgette Heyer’s novels is that her characters are always so well drawn, and I often take great pleasure in trying to puzzle them out. <br /><br />It was therefore with great pleasure that I discovered my suspicions about Sir Richard – suspicions that came to my mind in a pause between reading the chapters - had been right. He was indeed a romantic at heart, and deep down did want to be in love, and to marry a woman who cared for his character rather than his money. He was alike in some ways to Lord Rule, as I had previously asserted, but there were several key differences. Sir Richard, on top of being altogether too concerned with his appearance, was a rather more dashing hero on the surface. His exploits were decidedly more showy than those of the Earl of Rule, who preferred to operate mostly in the background and take great pleasure in doing so. Sir Richard also – despite having the fair share of gallantry necessary in most if not all heroes – often had no compunction about being rude… at the very least dangerously blunt or wilfully provoking. His liveliness, wit, humour and tolerance balanced with the aforementioned qualities made him an eminently satisfying hero for the story.<br /><br />However, I must confess that if I were in love with a man, I should not like to be called a “brat” by him as many times as Penelope (Pen) was named as such by Sir Richard. Of course it was a long time before the romance blossomed, and the term was for the most part used as an endearment, but I still found it very easy to wish that Sir Richard had come up with some other epithet for Miss Penelope Creed than “brat”. But in his defence; when a young lady drops out of a window into your drunken arms to escape a marriage with her cousin, thus giving you an excuse to escape the possibility of your own loveless marriage and taking you on something that cannot but be called an adventure… Well, I must ask, what else are you to call her? <br /><br />Penelope is one of the most adorable characters I’ve ever come across. Her endless enthusiasm and curiosity are so endearing, as is her trusting and kind nature. Her imagination runs riot through her knack of concocting stories to explain her presence in certain places, and one cannot help being in sympathy with Sir Richard, even as you laugh at his exasperation in having to go along with all of Pen’s stories; in most of which he figures as a cruel oppressor. Poor thing! Pen is a decidedly clever and determined girl, but can be a little clueless about the ways of the world sometimes. However, she is only seventeen, spirited and fond of adventure, so a little cluelessness is to be expected. And of course, she is brought to her senses at the most inopportune moment, which was rather sad, really. <br /><br />The characters that conspire to bring Penelope to her senses are Piers Luttrell – her supposed childhood sweetheart – and Cedric Brandon, who is in Somerset trying to discover what has happened to his brother Beverley Brandon. You know, I never thought I’d find someone who fulfilled the requirements of “odious little toad” any better than Mr Crosby Drellincourt from <em>The Convenient Marriage</em>. I congratulate Ms Heyer on having been able to create someone I actually despise more than Crosby – who I must admit did have some amusement value in his favour. Without going into particulars, in is perhaps fitting that Beverley came off far worse than Crosby.<br /><br />In any case, I was speaking of Piers and Cedric. Piers was a disappointing character to say the least. Well, of course he would be disappointing next to the endlessly amusing and perfectly lovely Sir Richard, but any man who can defend such a useless, pathetic creature as Lydia has got to have something wrong with him. The reader expects more from him because it seems throughout the story that <em>Pen</em> expected more from him, but in the end? Well, I honestly didn’t care about him that much. Seriously Piers, if you want to run off with a silly and shallow girl, that’s your own affair, but for God’s sake stop telling Pen about the <em>impropriety</em> of her situation! And Cedric was even worse. Between the two of them, Piers and Cedric manage to almost completely destroy Penelope’s illusions, and her happiness. I just wanted to push them both away and give Pen a hug, seeing her crushed under the knowledge that she is in love with Sir Richard, and at the same time convinced he only wants to marry her because it is the most correct thing to do.<br /><br />Now then, the ending; well, I must admit that, though being perfectly sweet and lovely, it did leave me feeling just very slightly dissatisfied. This was no doubt on account of the final chapter being such a… a whirlwind, I suppose. The first half of the chapter was everything that it should have been, worthy of all the tears I shed over it (that letter… *sniffles*) but the second half of the final chapter… It was a little confusing. People were running about here and there, with quite unnecessary disturbances, and the story finished within two pages of Richard and Pen being reunited. Everything was rounded up nicely enough, and it still made me laugh and smile, but I think the book would not have suffered from another ten pages or so to bring it to a more graceful ending. And perhaps it is silly of me, but I felt a childish disappointment in the fact that for the entire duration of the novel, Sir Richard had never seen Penelope dressed as a lady, instead of pretending to be a boy. In any case, all it took was remembering the rest of the novel to assuage my slight disappointment, so I bear Ms Heyer no lasting ill will for the feeling of being rushed towards the end of the story.<br /><br />Despite the hurried ending, <em>The Corinthian</em> really was amazingly fun. It’s also one of Heyers slightly shorter novels, so generally it doesn’t suffer from narrative sequences that are slightly too long, which I have come across in a few of her other, longer works. <em>The Corinthian</em> made me laugh all the time, it was very sweet, and you cannot help but love both Sir Richard and Penelope. The romance is somewhat more subtle in this novel than some, and doesn’t start be realized by the characters until late, but it was lovely and everything it should have been. And, let’s face it; we don’t need a really obvious romance all the time, do we? Sometimes we just want to find something romantic yet light and fun and hilarious, and that’s exactly what I found in <em>The Corinthian</em>. :)<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11191340284616682588">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14317546961866219920">I listened to the audio version, newly released at Audible. The narrator, Georgina Sutton, has a lovely British accent, and portrays Pen beautifully, and Richard fairly well. However, she makes the listening experience unpleasant to my ears for some of the secondary male characters. Hard on the ears. Raspy, scratchy, twangy, and in Cedric's case, also goofy.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14317546961866219920">I listened to the audio version, newly released at Audible. The narrator, Georgina Sutton, has a lovely British accent, and portrays Pen beautifully, and Richard fairly well. However, she makes the listening experience unpleasant to my ears for some of the secondary male characters. Hard on the ears. Raspy, scratchy, twangy, and in Cedric's case, also goofy. I think she mispronounced a few words: inebriated, babble (unless the British pronunciation differs from American English).<br /><br /> I'd go 3.5 stars for the narration, I guess.<br /><br />As for the story, 4.5 stars. A favorite. So much fun! It always amazed me how Heyer could write such a wide variety of romance novels. This one feels suspenseful yet lighthearted and adventurous. A run-away, a masquerade, a robbery, murder, and a rescue. Loved this romantic escapade. As with everything Heyer writes, the romance is clean and the relationships develop naturally. Also, the plot is sound, and the secondary characters are nicely textured, adding a lot to the enjoyment. Final scene is funny, especially considering the societal norms of the time. ;-)</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/11155721-charlotte" class="user" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=summer-2012" class="actionLinkLite">summer-2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=re-read" class="actionLinkLite">re-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=heyer" class="actionLinkLite">heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=4-stars" class="actionLinkLite">4-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=regency-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">regency-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11155721-charlotte?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer383076697">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16228698353382849880">The Corinthian, ironically, had made little and immense impact upon me when I first read it a few years ago. Whilst I didn’t rate it as one of her better novels and swiftly forgot its plot, it has this wonderful and memorable <em>”Let them look.”</em> moment that I always associate with Heyer’s regency romances… Little and immense indeed!<br /><br />Heyer is the only author I’ve discovered who can stand, for me, on par with the Austen classics and, whilst this isn’t one of my favourites (These Old Shades, Regency Bu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16228698353382849880">The Corinthian, ironically, had made little and immense impact upon me when I first read it a few years ago. Whilst I didn’t rate it as one of her better novels and swiftly forgot its plot, it has this wonderful and memorable <em>”Let them look.”</em> moment that I always associate with Heyer’s regency romances… Little and immense indeed!<br /><br />Heyer is the only author I’ve discovered who can stand, for me, on par with the Austen classics and, whilst this isn’t one of my favourites (These Old Shades, Regency Buck) it is far too engaging not to capture you regardless of how farfetched their adventures.<br /><br />The initial two chapters, prior to Pen literally jumping into the scene, are slow-going, but I suspect in some ways this is the point. Sir Wyndham is bored and disillusioned with the world, it holds no particular joy or exhilaration for him; these chapters capture quite how bleak he foresaw his future… And then Pen thrusts upon him all the excitement and sparkle that his life is missing.<br /><br />Pen is an absolute whirlwind, a force to be reckoned with. She’s trusting and friendly, almost to a fault, and, since she is not yet out, her lack of worldliness and youthful naivety do occasionally pitch her in the light of one much younger. This is, however, part of her charm as well as her emotional maturing during their escapades. I particularly love, at one point in the novel, her scolding of a typically tearful stereotype, pointing out the flaws that readers often pick up on (If you are upset, who cares if sitting on the grass might stain your dress?!)<br /><br />I wouldn’t recommend this as the first book for someone new to Heyer, however fans of <a title="The Foundling by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311122.The_Foundling">The Foundling</a>, <a title="The Masqueraders by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311201.The_Masqueraders">The Masqueraders</a> and <a title="Faro's Daughter by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311163.Faro_s_Daughter">Faro's Daughter</a> will almost certainly enjoy the romp… As per any Heyer book, the detail and research of the period is amazing, it’s a joy to read, and I know for certain that I’ll be chuckling over ‘That Waistcoat’ comedy for quite some time.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16228698353382849880">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10494304566270396232">After re-reading this, I've decided that <a title="The Corinthian by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian">The Corinthian</a>is one of my top-tier favorite <a title="Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">Georgette Heyer</a>s. Sir Richard Wyndham is one of Heyer's perfectly formed, well-bred, fashion sense-gifted, wealthy heroes who is tired of his life. Sir Richard has just resigned himself to the marriage his family is pushing him into when he runs into young Penelope Creed, a friendly, talkative heiress, who is literally running away from the marriage her own family is forcing on her. Sir Richard decides to help</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10494304566270396232">After re-reading this, I've decided that <a title="The Corinthian by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian">The Corinthian</a>is one of my top-tier favorite <a title="Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">Georgette Heyer</a>s. Sir Richard Wyndham is one of Heyer's perfectly formed, well-bred, fashion sense-gifted, wealthy heroes who is tired of his life. Sir Richard has just resigned himself to the marriage his family is pushing him into when he runs into young Penelope Creed, a friendly, talkative heiress, who is literally running away from the marriage her own family is forcing on her. Sir Richard decides to help Pen, who is disguised as a boy, on her journey, and he becomes a nicer man as a result. In some Heyer novels, the supporting characters provide much of the delight of the story, but in this one, Pen and Sir Richard are entertaining all by themselves.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1424575767">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424575767" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/875001-corinne" class="left imgcol" title="Corinne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220232981p2/875001.jpg" alt="Corinne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1424575767?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/875001-corinne" class="user" title="Corinne">Corinne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1424575767">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2404554584457740238">Lord Richard Wyndham is a Corinthian - a man with the finest principles, dressed in the finest styles. He takes pride in his independent nature and his solid common sense - not to mention his wicked grasp of cravat-tying. So when his mother and sister harass him about finding a wife, he wants nothing of it. Soon enough, though, he is on the brink of giving in when the adventure of a lifetime drops, literally, into his arms. From the seat of a stage coach to a woodland crime scene, Lord Richard's</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2404554584457740238">Lord Richard Wyndham is a Corinthian - a man with the finest principles, dressed in the finest styles. He takes pride in his independent nature and his solid common sense - not to mention his wicked grasp of cravat-tying. So when his mother and sister harass him about finding a wife, he wants nothing of it. Soon enough, though, he is on the brink of giving in when the adventure of a lifetime drops, literally, into his arms. From the seat of a stage coach to a woodland crime scene, Lord Richard's skills as a Corinthian have never been so needed. <br /><br />Delightful. This book had me chuckling out loud at both Lord Richard as well as the young-woman-in-disguise whose company he joins. Heyer's conversational banter can be so witty, her characters so full of life that it is just a joy to read her stories. Seriously, Richard's penchant for tying the perfect cravat had me almost in hysterics. I loved the slow romance of this one and my only complaint is that it ended too soon! I wanted more! I don't love all of her books but The Corinthian is exactly the style I love - uproarious, romantic and sharply witty. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2404554584457740238">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">high school and up</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer756867943">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9965720092969081622">I can't fathom why none of Georgette Heyer's books have been put to screen. Her dialogue is so vivid that I read it in my head with different voices, inflections, and even dramatic pauses. Her witty, natural banter makes it impossible not to do so. "The Corinthian" is one of her best for vivid dialogue even though the plot is very much like her other books; but since I can't seem to get enough of Heyer, then I'm okay with that.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1391923365">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391923365" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12138118-fiona" class="left imgcol" title="Fiona"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435012551p2/12138118.jpg" alt="Fiona" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1391923365?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12138118-fiona" class="user" title="Fiona">Fiona</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/319033.The_Corinthian" title="Paperback 9780099468080" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12138118-fiona?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12138118-fiona?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12138118-fiona?shelf=action-adventure" class="actionLinkLite">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12138118-fiona?shelf=drama" class="actionLinkLite">drama</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12138118-fiona?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1391923365">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14935018328990356845"><blockquote> <strong> <em>"I dare say," said Louisa, "that you are wondering what we are here for."<br />"I never waste my time in idle speculation," replied Sir Richard gently. "I feel sure that you are going to tell me what you are here for."<br />"Mama and I have come to speak to you about your marriage," said Louisa, taking the plunge.</em> </strong> </blockquote><br />Sir Richard Wyndham is rich and bored, on the verge of tying the knot in a marriage of convenience, and very drunk. When a girl disguised as a boy climbs out of a window and drops into his arms</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14935018328990356845"><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"I dare say," said Louisa, "that you are wondering what we are here for."<br />"I never waste my time in idle speculation," replied Sir Richard gently. "I feel sure that you are going to tell me what you are here for."<br />"Mama and I have come to speak to you about your marriage," said Louisa, taking the plunge.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br />Sir Richard Wyndham is rich and bored, on the verge of tying the knot in a marriage of convenience, and very drunk. When a girl disguised as a boy climbs out of a window and drops into his arms, an adventure begins which is to drag him all over the countryside and leave him mourning his desecrated reputation. But the most reckless decision of his life may turn out to be the best he ever made.<br /><br />A cute and rather silly story, involving plenty of running away, disguises, diamonds, forced marriages, elopements, crooks and crimes, awful relatives, and increasingly absurd plot entanglements (perhaps the typical fantasy shared by frustrated young women living tedious and restricted lives in the 19th century), all laced with that old-fashioned conviction, "all for honour's sake". Besides the highly unlikely but completely predictable romance, the plot was juvenile and boisterous; for me, what redeemed it was the comedic element - charming dialogue, some funny moments and the complete ludicrousness of it all.<br /><br />Apart from the deprivation of character development or the portrayal of anything resembling real life (except, perhaps, some general observations of people and society), I disliked the fact that this book doesn't discourage the temptation to every young girl to climb out a window and run away in search of adventure because her family doesn't suit her, not to mention trusting herself completely into the power or influence of an older man, especially one who is a total stranger and 12 years older (mild paedophilia?); the heroine never thinks before she does anything, let alone considers the repercussions of her actions on others; her selfishness and thoughtlessness is dressed up as "spirit" and "adventure"; and the notion that one can seriously fall in love in three days, let alone make a serious commitment for life to a man one hardly knows, all at the age of seventeen (I can't even think of her as <em>that</em> mature: she acts more like a fourteen-year-old). It's all too impossible to believe, but it worries me that to a 14-year-old it may not be all that impossible to believe.<br /><br />In terms of writing style, Heyer has a certain charm, but nothing stands out or really draws you in. Kudos to her for the details and the research involved (I didn't realise she lived a century after the era she wrote about; she was fairly convincing), and the ease with which she writes in that formal, old-fashioned voice.<br /><br />I would only recommend this book for 10- to 14-year-olds, but even then I doubt it's completely harmless or innocent of feeding the immature and impressionable sensibilities of teenage girls.<br /><br />Other than that, a light, fluffy story with a few laughs between the covers, some witty moments and a sunny ending. After hearing so many good things about <a title="Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">Georgette Heyer</a>, I did expect better, but I won't dismiss her entirely.<br /><br />An entertaining read, but Shakespeare's <a title="Twelfth Night by William Shakespeare" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1625.Twelfth_Night">Twelfth Night</a> tells the story much better.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"Never saw him until that night?" repeated Cedric, dazed.<br />"No! It was all chance, wasn't it, Richard?"<br />"It was," agreed Sir Richard, who seemed to be amused. "She dropped out of a window into my arms, Ceddie."<br />"She dropped out of––give me some more burgundy!" said Cedric.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14935018328990356845">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When Tom Conroy, a distant cousin and the new Earl of Clanross, appears after a year\'s delay, Elizabeth offers him a cool welcome. He is a dull stick and ill-mannered to boot. Yet he is the only man who has shown respect for her astronomical work, and his concern for her younger sisters\' welfare reveals a different side to him. Lord Bevis presses his suit with Lady Elizabeth, until she agrees, at long last, to marry him. She resists making an announcement, though, until he tells his somewhat traditional father that he will not only be marrying an heiress but her telescope. Elizabeth discovers a comet. Clanross proclaims his pride in her accomplishment, but Lord Bevis\'s reaction is far more traditional. Willoughby introduces a beautiful woman into the mix and the twins further complicate it.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14284113914135848148">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14284113914135848148">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14284113914135848148">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1364554-the-corinthian">Quotes from The Corinthian</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Sir Richard sighed. "Rid yourself of the notion that I cherish any villainous designs upon your person," he said. "I imagine I might well be your father. How old are you?"<br /><br />"I am turned seventeen."<br /><br />"Well, I am nearly thirty," said Sir Richard.<br /><br />Miss Creed worked this out. "You couldn't possibly be my father!"<br /><br />"I am far too drunk to solve arithmetical problems. Let it suffice that I have not the slightest intention of making love to you.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/309896-sir-richard-sighed-rid-yourself-of-the-notion-that-i" class="actionLinkLite">45 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I see now that there is a great deal in what Aunt Almeria says. She considers that there are terrible pitfalls in Society."<br /><br />Sir Richard shook his head sadly. "Alas, too true!"<br /><br />"And vice," said Pen awfully. "Profligacy, and extravagance, you know."<br /><br />"I know."<br /><br />She picked up her knife and fork again. "It must be very exciting," she said enviously.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/770326-i-see-now-that-there-is-a-great-deal-in" class="actionLinkLite">7 likes</a>
            </nobr>
